3:T46b,Recent advancements in natural language tasks leverage the emergent In-Context Learning (ICL) ability of pretrained Large Language Models (LLMs). ICL enables LLMs to perform new tasks by utilizing a limited number of input-output examples as prompts. While ICL circumvents the costly step of finetuning LLMs, its effectiveness is heavily dependent on the quality and ordering of provided examples (called exemplars). In this work, we propose a two-stage data-efficient framework Div-S3 for exemplar selection for ICL. The first stage focuses on data annotation and employs a pool-based active learning approach to select a set of Div erse and informative exemplars from the target tasks’ unlabeled pool. Given a test input/query, the second stage uses Submodular Span Summarization ( S3 ) to select the most relevant and non-redundant exemplars from the annotated pool of a limited budget. On 7 different NLP datasets and 5 LLMs of varying complexities, we show Div-S3 outperforms (1) existing active learning-based methods for data annotation for ICL and (2) similarity-based methods for test query-specific exemplars retrieval.4:T481,Recently, instruction-tuned large language models (LLMs) are showing prominent performance on various tasks, such as question answering. However, the majority of instruction-tuned LLMs are English-centric, which hinders their application to low-resource language QA. In this paper, we propose COde-Mixed Multi-lingual Instruction Tuning (COMMIT) to adapt English-centric LLM to low-resource language QA. We point out two main causes of English-centricness: imbalance of unlabeled data, and English-centric instruction tuning datasets. To deviate from English-centric instruction tuning, we propose to specialize code-mixing for instruction tuning, which blocks code-mixing in English templates, to leverage the potential of its superiority. To overcome data imbalance, we perform cross-lingual alignment. The majority of cross-lingual alignment works focused on making representations similar, which is not desirable to decoder-based LLMs, such as LLaMA. Therefore, we propose code-mixed continual causal language modeling to align the decoder. COMMIT improves the exact match score of low-resourced language QA by up to 32x. Code is publicly available.5:T4f9,Large multimodal models suffer from multimodal hallucination, where they provide incorrect responses misaligned with the given visual information. Recent works have conjectured that one of the reasons behind multimodal hallucination is due to the vision encoder failing to ground on the image properly. To mitigate this issue, we propose a novel approach that leverages self-feedback as visual cues. Building on this approach, we introduce Volcano, a multimodal self-feedback guided revision model. Volcano generates natural language feedback to its initial response based on the provided visual information and utilizes this feedback to self-revise its initial response. Volcano effectively reduces multimodal hallucination and achieves state-of-the-art on MMHal-Bench, POPE, and GAVIE. It also improves on general multimodal abilities and outperforms previous models on MM-Vet and MMBench. Through qualitative analysis, we show that Volcano’s feedback is properly grounded on the image than the initial response. This indicates that Volcano can provide itself with richer visual information through feedback generation, leading to self-correct hallucinations. We publicly release our model, data, and code at https://github.com/kaistAI/Volcanogithub.com/kaistAI/Volcano6:T4fa,Recently, large pre-trained language models (LLMs) have demonstrated superior language understanding abilities, including zero-shot causal reasoning. However, it is unclear to what extent their capabilities are similar to human ones. We here study the processing of an event B in a script-based story, which causally depends on a previous event A. In our manipulation, event A is stated, negated, or omitted in an earlier section of the text. We first conducted a self-paced reading experiment, which showed that humans exhibit significantly longer reading times when causal conflicts exist (\neg A \rightarrow B) than under logical conditions (A \rightarrow B). However, reading times remain similar when cause A is not explicitly mentioned, indicating that humans can easily infer event B from their script knowledge. We then tested a variety of LLMs on the same data to check to what extent the models replicate human behavior. Our experiments show that 1) only recent LLMs, like GPT-3 or Vicuna, correlate with human behavior in the \neg A \rightarrow B condition. 2) Despite this correlation, all models still fail to predict that nil \rightarrow B is less surprising than \neg A \rightarrow B, indicating that LLMs still have difficulties integrating script knowledge.7:T4ca,Large Language Models (LLMs) have been exhibiting outstanding abilities to reason around cognitive states, intentions, and reactions of all people involved, letting humans guide and comprehend day-to-day social interactions effectively. In fact, several multiple-choice questions (MCQ) benchmarks have been proposed to construct solid assessments of the models’ abilities. However, earlier works demonstrate the presence of inherent “order bias” in LLMs, posing challenges to the appropriate evaluation. In this paper, we investigate LLMs’ resilience abilities through a series of probing tests using four MCQ benchmarks. Introducing adversarial examples, we show a significant performance gap, mainly when varying the order of the choices, which reveals a selection bias and brings into discussion reasoning abilities. Following a correlation between first positions and model choices due to positional bias, we hypothesized the presence of structural heuristics in the decision-making process of the LLMs, strengthened by including significant examples in few-shot scenarios. Finally, by using the Chain-of-Thought (CoT) technique, we elicit the model to reason and mitigate the bias by obtaining more robust models.8:T57d,Large Language Models (LLM) have demonstrated their strong ability in the field of machine translation, yet they suffer from high computational cost and latency. Therefore, transferring translation knowledge from giant LLMs to medium-sized machine translation models is a promising research direction. However, traditional knowledge distillation methods ignore the capability of student and teacher models, therefore repeatedly teaching student models on the knowledge they have learned, and failing to extend to novel contexts and knowledge. In this paper, we propose a framework called MT-Patcher, which transfers knowledge from LLMs to existing MT models in a selective, comprehensive and proactive manner. Considering the current translation ability of student MT models, we only identify and correct their translation errors, instead of distilling the whole translation from the teacher. Leveraging the strong language abilities of LLMs, we instruct LLM teachers to synthesize diverse contexts and anticipate more potential errors for the student. Experiment results on translating both specific language phenomena and general MT benchmarks demonstrate that finetuning the MT model on about 10% examples can achieve comparable results to the traditional knowledge distillation method, and synthesized potential errors and diverse contexts further improve MT performances on unseen contexts and words.9:T476,Headline Generation is an essential task in Natural Language Processing (NLP), where models often exhibit limited ability to accurately interpret numerals, leading to inaccuracies in generated headlines. This paper introduces CoT-NumHG, a training strategy leveraging the Chain of Thought (CoT) paradigm for Supervised Fine-Tuning (SFT) of large language models. This approach is aimed at enhancing numeral perception, interpretability, accuracy, and the generation of structured outputs. Presented in SemEval-2024 Task 7 (task 3): Numeral-Aware Headline Generation (English), this challenge is divided into two specific subtasks. The first subtask focuses on numerical reasoning, requiring models to precisely calculate and fill in the missing numbers in news headlines, while the second subtask targets the generation of complete headlines. Utilizing the same training strategy across both subtasks, this study primarily explores the first subtask as a demonstration of our training strategy. Through this competition, our CoT-NumHG-Mistral-7B model attained an accuracy rate of 94%, underscoring the effectiveness of our proposed strategy.a:T4be,In this work, we propose a new task, compositional structured explanation generation (CSEG), to facilitate research on compositional generalization in reasoning. Despite the success of language models in solving reasoning tasks, their compositional generalization capabilities are under-researched. Our new CSEG task tests a model’s ability to generalize from generating entailment trees with a limited number of inference steps – to more steps, focusing on the length and shapes of entailment trees. CSEG is challenging in requiring both reasoning and compositional generalization abilities, and by being framed as a generation task. Besides the CSEG task, we propose a new dynamic modularized reasoning model, MORSE, that factorizes the inference process into modules, where each module represents a functional unit. We adopt modularized self-attention to dynamically select and route inputs to dedicated heads, which specializes them to specific functions. Using CSEG, we compare MORSE to models from prior work. Our analyses show that the task is challenging, but that the dynamic reasoning modules of MORSE are effective, showing competitive compositional generalization abilities in a generation setting.b:T4c6,Causal language models such as the GPT series have achieved significant success across various domains. However, their application to the lexical substitution task (LST) remains largely unexplored due to inherent limitations in autoregressive decoding. Our work is motivated by our observation that existing LST approaches tend to suffer from a misalignment between the pre-training objectives of the language models that they employ, and their subsequent fine-tuning and application for substitute generation. We introduce PromptSub, the first system to use causal language modeling (CLM) for LST. Through prompt-aware fine-tuning, PromptSub not only enriches the given context with additional knowledge, but also leverages the unidirectional nature of autoregressive decoding. PromptSub consistently outperforms GeneSis, the best previously published supervised LST method. Further analysis demonstrates the potential of PromptSub to further benefit from increased model capacity, expanded data resources, and retrieval of external knowledge. By framing LST within the paradigm of CLM, our approach indicates the versatility of general CLM-based systems, such as ChatGPT, in catering to specialized tasks, including LST.c:T42e,As generated text becomes more commonplace, it is increasingly important to evaluate how well-supported such text is by external knowledge sources. Many approaches for evaluating textual support rely on some method for decomposing text into its individual subclaims which are scored against a trusted reference. We investigate how various methods of claim decomposition—especially LLM-based methods—affect the result of an evaluation approach such as the recently proposed FActScore, finding that it is sensitive to the decomposition method used. This sensitivity arises because such metrics attribute overall textual support to the model that generated the text even though error can also come from the metric’s decomposition step. To measure decomposition quality, we introduce an adaptation of FActScore, which we call DecompScore. We then propose an LLM-based approach to generating decompositions inspired by Bertrand Russell’s theory of logical atomism and neo-Davidsonian semantics and demonstrate its improved decomposition materially affect LLM training, or is it mostly a negligible implementation detail. Many studies hold the tokenizer fixed and move on, but that hides potentially large differences in sequence length, compression, morphology handling, and multilingual balance.","importance":"This is directly relevant to pretraining. The tokenizer sits between data and model and therefore affects information density per token, context utilization, embedding and softmax cost, and cross-lingual fairness. If tokenizer choice matters a lot, then many scaling comparisons need to be reinterpreted under tokenization-aware normalization. If it matters little, that result is also important because it bounds how much engineering effort should be spent there.","technical_approach":"The likely contribution is a controlled empirical study comparing tokenizer choices while holding the rest of the training stack as constant as possible. A useful analysis would also examine token fertility, average sequence length, convergence speed, embedding overhead, and effects on rare words or morphologically rich languages. That is what separates a real tokenizer study from anecdotal preprocessing experiments. If retrieval can provide good proposals in repetitive domains, the serving stack becomes simpler and cheaper.","technical_approach":"REST uses retrieval-based speculative decoding: instead of asking a small model to propose future tokens, it retrieves similar contexts from a datastore and uses their continuations as draft candidates, which the main model then verifies in parallel. This work proposes using a residual energy-based model to capture the distributional shift from the base LLM to the aligned distribution.","importance":"A method-level contribution at the pretrain-posttrain interface. The goal is to recover a better quality-efficiency frontier.","importance":"This is method-level work with direct relevance to alternative language modeling paradigms beyond next-token autoregression. For pretraining researchers, it is useful because it shows how diffusion-style discrete generation can become more practical in seq2seq settings when combined with training schemes that reduce optimization difficulty.","technical_approach":"The method, Diffusion Glancing Transformer, combines iterative diffusion-based refinement with glancing training. Glancing exposes part of the ground-truth target during training so the model does not have to solve full parallel generation from scratch, while diffusion refines the sequence across steps and reduces the multimodality problem of one-shot prediction. For practitioners, this is a concrete recipe for reducing cross-lingual disparity with less disruption than redesigning the model.","technical_approach":"The core idea is a cross-lingual self-distillation framework with explicit teacher language selection. Instead of always distilling from English or from an aggregate multilingual teacher, the method chooses a more suitable teacher language for each target language, then uses the model’s own stronger predictions in that teacher language as supervision for the weaker target language. This differs from standard KD because it is not a larger model teaching a smaller one; it is the same multilingual model transferring knowledge across language views. It also differs from translation-based augmentation because the main mechanism is behavioral alignment, not simply more parallel data. Zuidema","Jaap Jumelet"],"institutions":[],"abstract":"In recent years, many interpretability methods have been proposed to help interpret the internal states of Transformer-models, at different levels of precision and complexity. Here, to analyze encoder-decoder Transformers, we propose a simple, new method: DecoderLens. Inspired by the LogitLens (for decoder-only Transformers), this method involves allowing the decoder to cross-attend representations of intermediate encoder layers instead of using the final encoder output, as is normally done in encoder-decoder models. The method thus maps previously uninterpretable vector representations to human-interpretable sequences of words or symbols. We report results from the DecoderLens applied to models trained on question answering, logical reasoning, speech recognition and machine translation. competent. The key question is how to route each query to the right expert model only when the quality gain justifies the cost. Fixed-model deployment wastes input-level heterogeneity, while full ensembling overpays for redundancy.","importance":"Its main contribution is a realistic view of ensembling: use reward signals to decide which model should answer which input. This also connects to the pretrain-posttrain loop: if routing can reliably identify latent experts, training could potentially encourage specialization more explicitly.","technical_approach":"The method is a reward-guided routing framework for LLM ensembles. The important trade-off is between routing overhead and avoided generation cost. Compared with standard ensembling, it gives up exhaustive redundancy to improve the cost-quality frontier; the main failure mode is routing error, which can erase most of the gain.","experiments":"The experiments likely compare the proposed routing strategy against single-model baselines, random or heuristic routing, and full ensembles under matched budget settings. 或加 latent variable 来缓解，但往往是“多样性上去了，质量掉了”，因为模型没有真正学到保留信息同时鼓励多样化表达的机制。","importance":"这项工作的贡献偏方法级，重点是把 variational autoencoder 和 mutual information maximization 结合起来提升生成多样性。它对 pretrain 的直接冲击有限，因为更像一个 可以理解为一个强调变分潜变量有效性的生成框架：通过最大化潜变量与生成文本之间的互信息，避免 latent 被强大的 decoder 忽略。相比普通 VAE 文本生成，关键选择不是只靠 KL 正则维持潜空间，而是直接推动 latent 捕获对输出有区分度的信息。这样设计有效，因为多样性真正需要的是可控且有语义的变因；如果 latent 不承载信息，采样再花哨也只是扰动表面形式。与最接近已有方法相比，它的差异应在于 mutual information 目标的引入方式，以及如何在训练稳定性和表达能力之间做平衡。","experiments":"实验应集中在开放式生成或条件生成任务上的质量-多样性权衡，对比标准 Its direct impact on large-scale pretraining is limited, but it is relevant for alternative language modeling and latent-generation research because it addresses a core failure mode of VAE-style text models: the latent variable gets ignored. If the method works well, it is less a new paradigm than a reusable ingredient for more expressive generators.","technical_approach":"VOLTA appears to be a variational autoencoding framework that explicitly maximizes mutual information between the latent variable and generated text. The key idea is to force the latent code to carry output-relevant information instead of relying only on KL regularization, which often leads to posterior collapse under a strong decoder. This design is sensible because useful diversity requires semantically meaningful variation, not just noisier sampling.","experiments":"The experiments likely compare VOLTA with standard VAEs, autoregressive baselines, and other diversity-oriented methods on open-ended or conditional generation tasks. This matters because MCQ evaluation often assumes order invariance, while in practice generative LMs may exploit superficial positional cues rather than only the content of the options.","importance":"This is mainly an evaluation-method paper, not a new pretraining method. Its value is that it exposes a hidden source of variance in widely used LLM benchmarks; for pretraining research, that means some conclusions about knowledge, calibration, or instruction-following may partly reflect prompt-format bias instead of model capability.","technical_approach":"The approach is a controlled analysis of option-order sensitivity rather than a modeling contribution. The same question is evaluated under multiple permutations of the answer choices, which isolates the effect of presentation order while keeping semantics fixed; this is the right design if the goal is to separate true reasoning from shortcut reliance on position, label tokens, or answer length. While these LLM achieve surprisingly good results it is a challenge to use them on more constrained resources. Techniques to compress these LLM into smaller and faster models have emerged for English or Multilingual settings, but it is still a challenge for other languages. claim，再逐条验证，但大家往往默认 decomposition 这一步是可靠的，实际上它本身会显著影响最终分数。过去像 FActScore 这类方法更关注验证器质量，而较少追问“拆得对不对”；作者指出，如果分解错了，错误会被错误地归到生成模型头上。","importance":"这项工作的价值在于把一个被低估的评测噪声源单独拎出来分析。它对 LLM 评测和训练反馈都很关键，因为一旦 decomposition 不稳定，事实性分数就不再是干净监督信号，后续无论用于模型比较、蒸馏还是 RL 奖励都会受污染。对 pretrain/posttrain 接口的启示很直接：如果你准备用 claim-level factuality metric 做训练闭环，先验证 decomposition 的可靠性，否则优化可能在追逐评测器误差。","technical_approach":"方法上，作者系统比较不同的 claim decomposition 方法，特别是基于 LLM 的分解方式，并分析它们如何改变类似 FActScore 的整体评测结果。关键点不在于提出新的事实验证器，而是在评测流水线里把 decomposition 从默认前处理提升为核心变量。进一步地，作者还提出了一个改造版指标来衡量 decomposition 质量，目的就是把“生成模型错”和“分解器错”分开。这种设计有效，因为它把误差归因从黑箱总分拆成了可分析组件。","experiments":"摘要给出的核心结论是：FActScore 这类支持度评测对 decomposition 方法敏感，尤其是 LLM-based decomposition 会实质改变最终结果；也就是说，评测方差并不只来自验证阶段。作者还引入了适配后的分解质量测度来定量评估这一环节。摘要没有提供所比较的分解器数量、数据规模、具体敏感度数值和改造指标的详细定义，因此不能写更细的数字；但仅这一发现就足够重要，因为它直接影响事实性 benchmark 的可解释性和可用性。","authors_note":"机构：约翰霍普金斯大学。Mark Dredze、Benjamin Van Durme 都是信息抽取、事实性与鲁棒评测方向的知名作者，JHU 在该方向有长期积累。"},"summary_en":{"core_problem":"The paper targets a hidden source of error in factuality evaluation: many support metrics first decompose generated text into atomic claims and then verify them, but that decomposition step is usually treated as if it were reliable by default. The authors show that this assumption is unsafe. If decomposition is poor, the final score can wrongly attribute decomposition errors to the text generator.","importance":"This is an evaluation-methods contribution with direct implications for training and benchmarking. If factuality metrics are sensitive to claim decomposition, then those scores are not clean supervision signals. That matters not only for model comparison, but also for distillation, reward modeling, or RL pipelines that might optimize against such metrics. The practical lesson is simple: before using claim-level factuality scores in a feedback loop, validate the decomposition step itself.","technical_approach":"The paper systematically compares different claim decomposition methods, with special attention to LLM-based decomposers, and studies how those choices change evaluation outcomes such as FActScore. The important move here is conceptual: decomposition is elevated from a preprocessing detail to a first-class variable in the evaluation pipeline. The authors also introduce an adapted metric for measuring decomposition quality so that errors from the decomposer can be separated from errors by the generation model.","experiments":"The main empirical result is clear from the abstract: support metrics like FActScore are sensitive to the decomposition method used, and LLM-based decomposition can materially change evaluation outcomes. The paper also proposes a way to quantify decomposition quality directly. The abstract does not report the number of decomposers compared, dataset size, exact sensitivity values, or the full definition of the adapted metric, so those details should not be invented. Even without them, the conclusion is already important because it affects the reliability of factuality benchmarks.","authors_note":"Institution: Johns Hopkins University. Mark Dredze and Benjamin Van Durme are well-known researchers in information extraction, factuality, and robust evaluation, and JHU has a strong track record in this
